## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is central to constitutive modeling in materials science. Temperature typically modifies elastic modulus, yield strength, and flow behavior, while strain determines the deformation response.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * (c1 + c2 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with T-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (strain hardening in plastic regime)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2) (nonlinear stress-strain with hardening)
- Hollomon equation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (flow stress with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook flow stress: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with thermal term)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T**c3) (power-law thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating strain hardening)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * (1 - c2 * exp(c3 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with T-dependence)
- Linear thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus linear in T)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (Arrhenius-like thermal activation of flow)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Ludwik equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (yield stress + hardening with thermal effects)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 + c3 * T) (shifted power law with temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) (high-temperature deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (1 + c*T) or exp(c*T) multiplying strain terms
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) structure indicating asymptotic stress plateau
- Thermal softening → stress decreases with temperature, often as (1 - c*T^m) or exp(-c*T)
- Elastic-plastic transition → additive decomposition: linear term in epsilon plus power-law or saturating term
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with n typically between 0.1 and 0.5 for metals
- Separable temperature-strain coupling → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), multiplicative decomposition common in constitutive models
- High-temperature creep activation → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or sinh-based flow rules
- Yield stress offset → constant term c0 added to strain-dependent terms representing initial yield
